# [PROLOGUE](prologue.md) [Mues](Mues.md) of fire
To anyone I've [offended](offended.md), I just want to say I [reinvent](reinvent.md) electric cars and I'm sending people to Mars in a rocket ship. 
Did you think I was also gonna be a chill, normal [dude](dude.md)? 
Elon Musk, [Saturday Night Live](##注释1), May 8th, 2021. 

The people who are crazy enough to think they can change the world are the ones who do [Steve Jobs](##注释2).
Prologue, Muse of Fire, The playground. 

As a kid growing up in South Africa, Elon Musk knew pain and learned how to survive it. 
When he was 12, he was taken by bus to a wilderness survival camp known as a [veld](veld.md) school. 
It was a [paramilitary](paramilitary.md)[ Lord of the Flies](##注释3),she recalls. 
The kids were each given small [rations](ration.md) of food and water and they were allowed, even encouraged to fight over them. 
Bullying was considered a [virtue](virtue.md). 
His younger brother Kimbell says the big kids quickly learned to punch the little ones in the face and take their stuff.
Elon, who was small and emotionally awkward, got beaten up twice.
He would end up losing 10 pounds.
Near the end of the first week, the boys were divided into two groups and told to attack each other.
It was so [insane](insane.md), [mind-blowing](mind-blowing.md). Musk recalls, every few years, one of the kids would die.
The [counsellors](counsellor.md) would recount such stories as warnings.
"Don't be stupid like that [dumbfuck](dumb.md) (这里fuck值代那个死掉的人，代表鄙夷)who died last year," they would say.
"Don't be the weak dumbfuck."
 
The second time Elon went to veld school, he was about to turn 16.
He'd gotten much bigger, bursting up to 6 feet with a bear like[frame](frame.md) (这里是bear like，frame 身材), and he'd learned some [judo](judo.md).
So veld school wasn't so bad.
"I realized by then that if someone bullied me, I could punch them very hard in the nose, and then they wouldn't bully me again.
They might beat [the shit out of me] (打的我屁滚尿流), but if I had punched them hard in the nose, they wouldn't come after me again."
 
South Africa in the 1980s was a violent place with [machine gun] (机枪) attacks and knife killings common.
Once, when Elon and Kimbell got off a train on their way to an [anti-apartheid](apartheid.md) music concert, they had to [wade](wade.md) through a pool of blood next to a dead person with a knife still sticking out of his brain.
For the rest of the evening, the blood on the [soles](sole.md) of their [sneakers](sneaker.md) made a [sticky](sticky.md) sound against the pavement.
 
The Musk family kept German [shepherd](shepherd.md) dogs that were trained to attack anyone running by the house.
When he was 6, Elon was racing down the driveway, and his favorite dog attacked him, taking a massive bite out of his back.
In the emergency room, when they were preparing to [stitch](stitch.md) him up, he resisted being treated, until he was promised that the dog would not be punished.
"You're not gonna kill him, are you?" Elon asked, they swore that they wouldn't.
In recounting the story, Musk pauses and stares [vacantly](vacantly.md) for a very long time.
"Then they damn well shot the dog dead."
 
His most [searing](searing.md) experiences came at school.
For a long time, he was the youngest and smallest student in his class.
He had trouble picking up social [cues](cue.md) (这里指他不能理解别人的潜台词).
Empathy did not come naturally, and he had neither the desire nor the [instinct](instinct.md) to be [ingratiating](ingratiating.md).
As a result, he was regularly picked on by bullies who would come up And punch him in the face.
"If you've never been punched in the nose, you have no idea how it affects you the rest of your life," he says.
At [assembly](assembly.md) one morning, a student who was [horsing around](horsing%20around.md) with a gang of friends [bumped into](bump%20into.md) him.

Elon pushed him back.
[Words were exchanged] (这里指吵起来了).
The boy and his friends hunted Elon down at [recess](recess.md) and found him eating a sandwich.
They came up from behind, kicked him in the head and pushed him down a set of concrete steps.
"They sat on him and just kept beating the shit out of him and kicking him in the head," says Campbell.
"We've been sitting with him. When they got finished, I couldn't even recognize his face.
With such a [swollen](swollen.md) ball of flesh that you could barely see his eyes."
He was then taken to the hospital, was out of school for a week.
Decades later, he was still getting corrective surgery to try to fix the tissues inside his nose.
 
But those [scars](scar.md) were minor compared to the emotional ones [inflicted](inflict.md) by his father.
Mask, an engineer [robe](robe.md) and [charismatic](charismatic.md) [fantasist](fantasist.md).
But to this day, the devil's Elon.
 
After the school fight, [Arrow] [sided with] the kid who [pummeled](pummeled.md) Elon's face.
The boy had just lost his father to suicide and Elon had called him stupid.
Arrow says Elon had this tendency to call people stupid.
"How could I possibly blame that child?"
 
When Elon [[001_finally|finally]] came home from the [[001_hospital|hospital]], his father berated him.
"I had to stand for an hour as he yelled at me and called me an [[001_idiot|idiot]] and told me that I was just worthless," Elon recalls.
Campbell, who had to watch the [tirade](tirade.md), says it was the worst memory of his life.
"My father just lost it, Ballistic, as he often did. He had zero compassion."
 
Both Elon and Campbell, who no longer speak to their father, say his claim that Elon [provoked](provoked.md) the attack is [unhinged](unhinged.md) and that the [perpetrator](perpetrator.md) ended up being sent to [juvenile](juvenile.md) prison for.
They say their father is a [volatile](volatile.md) [fabulist](fabulist.md), regularly [spinning](spin.md) tales that are [larded](larded.md) with fantasies, sometimes calculated and at other times [delusional](delusional.md).
He has a [Jekyll and Hyde nature](##注释4), they say.
One minute he would be friendly, The next he would launch into an hour or more of unrelenting abuse.
He would In every tirade by telling Elon how [pathetic](pathetic.md) he was.
Elon would just have to stand there, not allowed to leave.
"It was mental [torture](torture.md)," Elon says, pausing for a long time and choking up slightly.
"He sure knew how to make anything terrible. What I call arrow, he talk, He talks to me for almost three hours and then follows up regularly with calls and texts.
 
Over the next two years, He's eager to describe and send me photos of the nice things he provided to his kids, at least during the periods when his engineering business was doing well.
At one point, he drove a [Rolls-Royce] (劳斯莱斯), built a wilderness [lodge](lodge.md) with his boys and got [raw](raw.md) [emeralds](emerald.md) from a mine owner in Zambia until that business collapsed.
But he admits that he encouraged a physical and emotional toughness.
"Their experiences with me would have made Vell school quite [tame](tame.md)," he says, adding that violence was simply part of the learning experience.
In South Africa, "Two held you down While another pummeled your face with a log and so on."
He says new boys Were forced to fight the school [thud](thud.md) on their first day at a new school.
He probably [concedes](concede.md) that he exercised an extremely [stern](stern.md) [streetwise](streetwise.md) [autocracy](autocracy.md) with his boys.
Then he makes a point of adding, "Elon would later apply that same stern autocracy to himself and others."
 
"[Adversity](adversity.md) shape me. Someone once said that every man is trying to live up to his father's expectations or make up for his father's mistakes," Barack Obama wrote in his memoirs.
"And I suppose that may explain my particular [malady](malady.md)."
 
In Elon Musk's case, his father's impact on his [psyche](psyche.md) would [linger](linger.md) [despite](despite.md) many attempts to banish him, both [physically](physically.md) and [psychologically](psychologically.md).
Elon's moods would cycle through light and dark, intense and [goofy](goofy.md), [detached](detached.md) and emotional, with occasional [plunges](plunge.md) into what those around him [dreaded](dreaded.md) as demon mode.
Unlike his father, he would be caring with his kids.
But in other ways, his behavior would [hint](hint.md) at a danger that needed to be constantly battled, the [specter](specter.md) that, as his mother put it, he might become his father.
Of the most [resident](resident.md) [tropes](trope.md) in [mythology](mythology.md), to what [extent](extent.md) does the [epic](epic.md) [quest](quest.md) of the [Star Wars](##注释5) hero require exercising the demons [bequeathed](bequeathed.md) by [Darth Vader](## 注释6) and wrestling with the dark side of the force?
 
With a childhood like his in South Africa, "I think you have to shut yourself down emotionally in some ways," says his first wife, Justine, the mother of five of his surviving 10 children.
"If your father is always calling you a [moron](moron.md) and an idiot, maybe the only response is to turn off anything inside that would have opened up an emotional dimension That he didn't have tools to deal with."
This emotional shut-off [valve](valve.md) could make him [callous](callous.md), but it also made him a risk-seeking innovator.
"He learned to shut down fear," Justin says.
"If you turn off fear, then maybe you have to turn off other things, like joy or empathy."
 
The PTSD from his childhood also [instilled](instil.md) in him an [aversion](aversion.md) to [contentment](contentment.md).
"I just don't think he knows how to savor success and smell the flowers," says Claire Bouchard, the artist known as [Grimes] (这是指她女友的艺名), who is the mother of three of his other children.
"I think he got [conditioned](conditioned.md) in childhood that life is pain."
 
Musk agrees.
"Adversity shape me," he says.
"My pain [Threshold](Threshold.md) became very high."
 
During a particularly hellish period of his life. In 2008, after the first three launches of his SpaceX rockets [exploded](explode.md) and Tesla was about to go [bankrupt](bankrupt.md), he would wake up [thrashing](thrashing.md) and recounted to Lula Riley, who became his second wife, the [horrendous](horrendous.md) things his father had once said.
"I'd heard him use those [phrases](phrase.md) himself," she says.
"It had a [profound](profound.md) effect on how he operates."
When he recalled these memories, he would [zone out](zone%20out.md) and seemed to disappear behind his steel-colored eyes.
"I think he wasn't conscious of how that still affected him because he thought of it as something in his childhood," Liley says.
"But he's retained a childlike, almost [stunted](stunted.md) side inside the man. Still, there is a child, a child standing in front of his dad."
 
Out of this [cauldron](cauldron.md), Musk developed an [aura](aura.md) that made him seem at times like an alien, as if his Mars mission were an [aspiration](aspiration.md) to return home and his desire to build [humanoid](humanoid.md) robots were a [quest](quest.md) for [kitsch](kitsch.md).
You'd not be totally shocked if he [ripped off](ripped%20off.md) his shirt and you discovered that he had no [naval](naval.md) and was not of this planet born.
But his childhood also made him all too human, a tough yet vulnerable boy who decided to embark on epic quest.
He developed a [fervor](fervor.md) that [cloaked](cloak.md) his [goofiness](goofiness.md) and a goofiness that cloaked his fervor.
Slightly uncomfortable in his own body. Like a big man who was never an athlete, he would walk with the [stride](stride.md) of a mission driven bear and dance [jigs](jig.md) That seemed taught by a robot with the [conviction](conviction.md) of a [prophet](prophet.md).
He would speak about the need, Need to [nurture](nurture.md) the [flame](flame.md) of human [consciousness](consciousness.md), [fathom](fathom.md) the universe and save our planet.
 
At first, I thought this was mainly role playing, the team boosting [pep](pep.md) talks and [podcast](podcaast.md) fantasies of a man child who had read the [Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy](##注释6) once too often.
But the more I encountered it, the more I came to believe that his sense of mission was part of what drove him.
While other entrepreneurs struggled to develop a world view, he developed a cosmic view.
His heritage and breeding along with the [hard wiring](hard%20wiring.md) of his brain made him at times callous and [impulsive](impulsive.md).
It all also led to an [exceedingly](exceedingly.md) high tolerance for risk.
He could calculate it coldly and also embrace it [feverishly](feverishly.md).
 
"Elon wants risk for its own [sake](sake.md)," says [Peter Thiel](##注释8), who became his partner in the early days of [PayPal](## 注释9).
"He seems to enjoy it, [indeed](indeed.md) at times be addicted to it.
He became one of those people who feels most alive when a hurricane is coming."
"I was born for a storm and a calm does not suit me," [Andrew Jackson](##注释10) once said.
[Likewise](likewise.md) with Musk, he developed a [siege](siege.md) [mentality](mentality.md) that included an attraction, sometimes a craving for storm and drama.
Both at work and in the romantic relationships he struggled and failed to maintain, He thrived.
"I've done crisis deadlines and wild(这里的wild表示狂野的失控的感觉) [surges](surges.md) of work.
When he face [torturous](torturous.md) challenges, the [strain](strain.md) would often keep him awake at night and make him [vomit](vomit.md).
But it also energized him.
"He's a drama magnet," says Campbell.
"That's his compulsion, the theme of his life."
 
When i was reporting on steve jobs, his partner, steve was in the said question to ask was, did he have to be so mean, so rough and cruel, so drama addicted?
When i turned the question back to wasas at the end of my reporting, he said that if he had run Apple,he would have been kinder.
He would have treated everyone there like family, and not [summarily](summarily.md) fired people.
Then he paused and added, but if I had run Apple, we may never have made the [Macintosh](##注释11)
And thus the question about Elon Musk, could he have been more chill, and still be the one launching us toward Mars and an electric vehicle future?
 
At the beginning of 2022, after a year marked by SpaceX making 31 successful rocket launches, Tesla selling close to a million cars, and him becoming the richest man on earth, Musk spoke ruefully about his compulsion to [stir](stir.md) up dramas.
"I need to shift my mindset away from being in crisis mode," he told me, "which it has been in for about 14 years now, or [arguably](arguably.md) most of my life."
It was a [wistful](wistful.md) comment, not a New Year's [resolution](resolution.md), even as he made the [pledge](pledge.md), he was secretly buying up [shares](share.md) of Twitter, the world's [ultimate](ultimate.md) playground.
 
That April, he snuck away to the Hawaiian house of his mentor, [Larry Ellison](##注释12), founder of [Oracle](##注释13), accompanied by the actress [Natasha Bassett](##注释14), an occasional girlfriend.
He'd been offered a [board seat] (这里指董事会席位) at Twitter, but over the weekend, he concluded that wasn't enough.
It was in his nature to want total control.
So he decided he challed the trigger on his plan and [went on] (这里指登上推特) Twitter.
["I made an offer,"] (这是在推特上发的消息，指马斯克宣布收购推特) he announced.
 
[Over the years](Over%20the%20year.md), whenever he was in a dark place or felt threatened, it took him back to the [horrors](horror.md) of being bullied on the playground.
Now he had the chance to own the playground

# Chapter one Advanturers
**Joshua and Winifred Haldeman**

Elon Musk's attraction to risk was a family [trait](trait.md).
In that [regard](regard.md), he took after his [maternal](maternal.md) grandfather, Joshua Haldeman, a [daredevil](daredevil.md)adventurer with strongly held opinions(执念), who was raised on a farm on the [barren](barren.md) plains of central Canada. 

He studied [chiropractic](chiropractic.md) techniques in [Iowa](lowa.md), then returned to his hometown near Moose Jaw, where he [broke](broke.md) in horses and gave chiropractic adjustments in exchange for food and lodging. 
He was eventually able to buy his own farm, but he lost it during the [depression of the 1930s.  1930大衰退
For the next few years, he worked as a cowboy, [rodeo](rodeo.md) performer, and construction hand.

His one [constant](constant.md) was a love for adventure. 
He married and divorced, traveled as a [hobo](hobo.md) on [freight](freight.md) [trains](train.md), and was a [stowaway](stowaway) on an [ocean-going](ocean-going.md) ship.
The loss of his farm [instilled](instill.md) in him a [populism](populism.md), and he became active in a movement known as the Social Credit Party, which [advocated](advocate.md) giving citizens free credit notes they could use like [currency](currency.md).
The movement had a [conservative](conservative.md) [fundamentalist](fundamentalist.md) [streak](streak.md) tinged with [anti-Semitism](Anti-Semitism.md). Its first leader in Canada [decried](decry.md) a [perversion](perversion.md) of cultural ideals because a [disproportionate](disproportionate.md) number of Jews occupy positions of control. 
Haldeman rose to become Chair of the party's national [council](council.md). 

He also [enlisted](enlist.md) in a movement called [technocracy](technocracy.md), which believed that government should be run by [technocrats](technocrat.md) rather than politicians. 
It was [temporarily](temporarily.md) [outlawed](outlaw.md) in Canada because of its opposition to the country's entry into World War II. 
Haldeman [defied](defy.md) the ban by taking out a newspaper ad supporting the movement.

At one point, he wanted to learn [ballroom](ballroom.md) dancing(社交舞), which is how he met Winifred Fletcher, whose adventurous streak was equal to his. 
As a 16-year-old, she got a job at the Moose Jaw Times-Herald, but she dreamed of being a dancer and actress. 
So, she [lit out](light%20out.md) by train to Chicago, and then New York City. 
Upon her return, she opened a dance school in Moose Jaw, which is where Haldeman showed up for lessons. 
When he asked her to dinner, she replied, "I don't date my clients." So, he quit the class, and asked her out again. 
A few months later, he asked, "when will you marry me?"
She responded, "tomorrow." 

They had four children including twin girls, May and K, born in 1948.
One day on a trip, he spotted a for-sale sign on a single-engine [Luscombe](Luscombe.md) airplane sitting in a farmer's field. 
He had no cash, but he convinced the farmer to take his car in exchange. 
It was rather [impetuous](inpetuous.md), since Haldeman did not know how to fly.
He hired someone to fly him home, and teach him how to [pilot](pilot.md) the plane.
The family came to be known as the flying Haldemans, and he was described by a [chiropractic](chiropractic.md) trade [journal](journal.md) as "perhaps the most remarkable figure in the history of flying chiropractors," a rather [narrow](narrow.md), [albeit](albeit.md) accurate [accolade](accolade.md). 

They bought a larger single-engine plane, a Belongia, when May and K were three.
With his [quirky](quirky.md) [conservative](conservative.md) populist views, Haldeman came to believe that the Canadian government was [usurping](usurp.md) too much control over the lives of individuals, and that the country had gone soft(软弱).
So in 1950, he decided to move to South Africa, which was still ruled by a white [apartheid](apartheid.md) [regime](regime.md). 
They [took apart](take%20apart.md) the Belonger, [crated](crate.md) it, and boarded a [freighter](freighter.md) for Cape Town.

Haldeman decided he wanted to live in an English-speaking area, so they took off toward Johannesburg, where most of the white citizens spoke English rather than Afrikaans.
But as they flew over nearby Pretoria, the [lavender](lavender.md) [jacaranda](jacaranda.md) flowers were in bloom, and Haldeman announced, "This is where we'll stay."

When Joshua and Winifred were young, a [charlatan](charlatan.md) named William Hunt, known at least to himself as the great Forini, came to Moose Jaw and told tales of an ancient lost city he had seen when crossing the Kalahari Desert in South Africa.
"This [fabulist](fabulist.md) showed my grandfather pictures that were obviously fake, but he became a believer and decided it was his mission to rediscover it," Musk says. 
Once in Africa, the Haldemans made a month-long [trek](trek.md) into the Kalahari every year to search for this legendary city.
They hunted for their own food and slept with their guns so they could [fend](fend.md) off lions. 
The family adopted a [motto](motto.md), "Live dangerously, carefully." (大胆的活，谨慎的行)

They embarked on long-distance flights to places such as Norway, [tied for](tie%20for.md) first place in the 12,000-mile Cape Town to Algiers [motor rally](motor%20rally.md), and became the first to fly a single-engine plane from Africa to Australia. 
"They had to remove the back seats to put in gas tanks," May later recalled.

Joshua Haldeman's risk-taking eventually caught up with him. 
He was killed when a person he was teaching to fly hit a [power line](power%20line.md), causing the plane to flip and crash. 
His grandson Elon was three at the time. 
"He knew that real adventures involve risk," he says. 
"Risk energized him." Haldeman [imprinted](imprint.md) that spirit onto one of his twin girls, Elon's mother, May. 
"I know that I can take a risk [as long as](as%20long%20as.md) I'm prepared," she says.

**May Haldeman and Errol Musk** 

As a young student, May did well in science and math.
She was also [strikingly](strikingly.md) good-looking, tall, blue-eyed, with high [cheekbones](cheekbone.md) and [sculpted](sculpted.md) [chin](chin.md). 
She began working at age 15 as a model, doing department store [runway](runway.md) shows on Saturday mornings.
Around that time, she met a boy in her neighborhood, who was also strikingly good-looking, [albeit](albeit.md) in a smooth and [catty](catty.md) way. 

Elon Musk's father, Errol, was an adventurer and wheeler dealer, always on the lookout for the next opportunity. 
His mother, May, was from England, where she finished school at 14, worked at a factory making skins for fighter [bombers](bomber.md), then took a [refugee](refugee.md) ship to South Africa. There, she met Walter Musk, a [cryptographer](cryptographer.md) and [military intelligence](military%20intellligence.md) officer, who worked in Egypt on [schemes](scheme.md) to fool the Germans by [deploying](deploy.md) fake weapons and [searchlights](searchlight.md). 
After the war, he did little [other than](other%20than.md) sit silently in an [armchair](armachair.md), drink, and use his cryptology skills on [crossword](crossword.md) puzzles. 
So, May left him, went back to England with their two sons, bought a [Buick](Buick.md), and then returned to Pretoria. 
"She was the strongest person I ever met," Errol says.

Errol earned a degree in engineering and worked on building hotels, shopping centers, and factories.
On the side, he liked restoring old cars and planes. 
He also [dabbled in](dabble.md) politics, defeating an Afrikaaner member of the pro-apartheid National Party to become one of the few English-speaking members of the Pretoria City Council. 
The Pretoria News for March 9th, 1970, reported the [election](election.md) under the headline, "Reaction against the [establishment](establishment.md)." 
Like the Haldemans, he loved flying. 
He bought a twin-engine Cessna Golden Eagle, which he used to [ferry](ferry.md) television crews to a [lodge](lodge.md) he had built in the bush.
On one trip in 1986, when he was looking to sell the plane, he landed at an [airstrip](airstrip.md) in Zambia, where a Panamanian-Italian [entrepreneur](entrepreneur.md) offered to buy it. 
They agreed on a price, and instead of taking payment in cash, Errol was given a [portion](portion.md) of the emeralds produced at three small mines that the entrepreneur owned in Zambia. 
Zambia then had a [postcolonial](postcolonial.md) black government, but there was no functioning [bureaucracy](bureaucracy.md), so the mine was not [registered](register.md). 
"If you registered it, you would [wind up](wind%20up.md) with nothing, because the blacks would take everything from you," Errol says. 
He criticizes May’s family for being racist, which he insists he is not. 
"I don't have anything against the blacks, but they are just different from what I am," he says in a [rambling](rambling.md) phone [discourse](discourse.md). 

Errol, who never had an [ownership](ownership.md) [stake](stake.md) in the mine, expanded his trade by importing [raw](raw.md) emeralds and having them cut in Johannesburg. 
"Many people came to me with stolen [parcels](parcel.md)," he says. 
"On trips overseas, I would sell emeralds to jewelers.
It was a cloak and [dagger](dagger.md) thing, because none of it was legal."
After producing profits of roughly $210,000, his emerald business collapsed in the 1980s when the Russians created [artificial](arificial.md) emeralds in the lab;
he lost all of his emerald earnings. 

**Their Marriage** 

Errol Musk and May Haldeman began dating when they were young teenagers. 
From the start, their relationship was filled with drama. 
He repeatedly [proposed](propose.md) to her, but she didn't trust him. 
When she discovered he was [cheating on](cheat%20on.md) her, she became so upset that she cried for a week and couldn't eat. 
"Because of [grief](grief.md), I dropped 10 pounds," she recalls. 
It helped her win a local beauty contest: she got $150 in cash, plus 10 tickets to a [bowling](bowling.md) [alley](alley.md), and became a finalist in the Miss South Africa contest. 

When May graduated from college, she moved to Cape Town to give talks about nutrition. 
Errol came to visit, brought an engagement [ring](ring.md), and proposed.
He promised he would change his ways and be [faithful](faithful.md) once they were married. 
May had just [broken off ](break%20off.md)a relationship with another unfaithful boyfriend, gained a lot of weight, and begun to fear that she would never get married, so she agreed.

The night of the wedding, Errol and May took an inexpensive flight to Europe for their honeymoon. 
In France, he bought copies of *Playboy* (banned in South Africa) and lay on the small hotel bed looking at them, [much to May's annoyance](much%20to.md). 
Their fights turned bitter. 
When they got back to Pretoria, she thought of trying to get out of the marriage, but she soon became [nauseated](nauseate.md) from [morning sickness](morning%20sickness.md).
She had become pregnant on the second night of their honeymoon, in the town of Nice. 
"It was clear that marrying him had been a mistake," she recalls. "But now it was impossible to [undo](undo.md)." 
# Chapter two a Mind of His Own
**In 1970s, lonely and determined**.
 
At 7:30 on the morning of June 28th, 1971, May Musk gave birth to an 8 - pound, 8 - [ounce](ounce.md) boy with a very large head. 
At first, she and Aaron were going to name him Nice after(根据) the town in France spelled N - I - C - E, where he was [conceived](conceive.md). 
History may have been different or at least [amused](amuse.md) if the boy had to go through life with the name Nice Musk. 
Instead, in the hope of making the Haldemans happy, Aaron agreed that the boy would have names from that side of the family, Elon, after May's grandfather, J. Elon Haldeman, and Reeve, the [maiden](maiden.md) name of May's maternal grandmother. 
Arol liked the name Elon because it was [biblical](biblical.md) and he later claimed that he had been present. 
As a child, he says he heard about a science fiction book by the rocket scientist Wernher von Braun called Project Mars, which describes a [colony](colony.md) on the planet run by an [executive](executive.md) known as the Elon.
 
Elon cried a lot, ate a lot and slept little. 
At one point, May decided to just let him cry until he fell asleep.
But she changed her mind after neighbors called the police. 
His moods switched rapidly.
When he wasn't crying, his mother says, he was really sweet.
 
Over the next two years, May had two more children, Kimber and Taska.
She didn't [cuddle](cuddle.md) them. 
They were allowed to [roam](roam.md) freely. 
There was no [nanny](nanny.md), just a housekeeper who paid little attention. 
When Elon began experimenting with rockets and [explosives](explosive.md), he says he's surprised he made it through childhood with all of his fingers intact.
 
When he was three, his mother decided that because he was so [intellectually](intellectually.md) curious, he should be in nursery school. 
The [principal](principal.md) tried to [dissuade](dissuade.md) her, they pointing out that being younger than anyone else in the class her year would present social challenges.
They should wait.
"I can't do that," May said. 
"He needs someone besides me to talk to. 
I really have this genius child." She [prevailed](prevailed.md). 
It was a mistake. 
Elon had no friends. 
And by the time he was in second grade, he was [tuning out](tuning%20out.md). 
The teacher would come up to me and yell at me, but I would not really see or hear her, he says.
His parents got called in to see the principal, who told them, "we have reason to believe that Elon is [retarded](retarded.md)." 
He spent most of his time in a [trance](trance.md), not listening, one of his teachers explained. 
"He looks out of the window all the time, and when I tell him to pay attention, he says, the leaves are turning brown." 
Now, Arrow replied that Elon was right. 
The leaves were turning brown. 
The [impasse](impasse.md) was broken when his parents agreed that Elon's hearing should be tested, [as if](as%20if.md) that might be the problem.
They decided it was an ear problem, so they took my [adenoids](adenoid.md) out, he said. 
That calmed down the school officials, but it did nothing to change his tendency to zone out and [retreat](retreat.md) into his own world when thinking. 
Ever since I was a kid, if I start to think about something hard, then all of my [sensory](sensory.md) systems turn off, he says. 
"I can't see or hear anything. 
I'm using my brain to [compute](compute.md), not for incoming information." 
The other kids would jump up and down and wave their arms in his face to see if they could [summon](summon.md) back his attention, but it didn't work. 
"It's best not to try to break through when he has that vacant stare," his mother says.
 
[Compounding](compound.md) his social problems was his unwillingness to suffer politely those he considered fools. 
He used the word "stupid" often. 
Once he started going to school, he became so lonely and sad, his mother says.
Kimber and Tosca would make friends on the first day, bring them home. 
But Elon never brought friends home.
He wanted to have friends, but he just didn't know how. 
As a result, he was lonely, very lonely. 
And that pain remained [seared into](sear%20into.md) his soul. 
When I was a child, there's one thing I said. 
He recalled in an interview with Rolling Stone during a [tumultuous](tumultuous.md) period in his love life in 2017.
"I never want to be alone. 
That's what I would say. I don't want to be alone."
 
One day when he was five, one of his cousins was having a birthday party, but Elon was punished for getting into a fight and told to stay home. 
He was a very determined kid and he decided to walk on his own to his cousin's house. 
The problem was that it was on the other side of Pretoria, a walk of almost two hours, hours plus.
He was too young to read the road signs.
"I kind of knew what the route looked like because I had seen it from a car.
And I was determined to get there. 
So I just start Walking."He says. 
He managed to arrive just as the party was ending. 
When his mother saw him coming down the road, she freaked out. 
Fearing he would be punished again, he climbed a [maple](maple.md) tree and refused to come down.
Kimber remember standing [beneath](beneath.md) the tree and staring at his older brother in [awe](awe.md). 
"He has this fierce determination that blows your mind and was sometimes frightening and still is."
 
When he was eight, he focused his determination on getting a motorcycle.
Yes. 
At age eight.
He would stand next to his father's chair and make his case over and over. 
When his father picked up a newspaper and ordered him to be quiet, Elon would continue to stand there. 
It just was [extraordinary](extraordinary.md) to watch this happen.
Kimber says. 
He would stand there silently, then [resume](resume.md) his argument, then stand silent. 
This happened every evening for weeks.
His father finally [caved](cave.md) and got Elon a blue and gold 50 cc Yamaha.
 
Elon also had a tendency to be [spacey](spacey.md) and wander off on his own, [oblivious](oblivious.md) to what others were doing. 
On a family trip to Liverpool to see some of their relatives when he was 8, his parents left him and his brother in a park to play by themselves. 
It was not in his nature to stay put, so he started wandering the streets. 
Some kid found me crying and took me to his mom who gave me milk and biscuits and called the police. 
He recalls. 
When he was reunited with his parents at the police station, he was unaware that anything was [amiss](amiss.md).
"It was [insane](insane.md) to leave me and my brother alone in the park at that age," he says. 
"But my parents weren't [overprotective](overprotective.md) like parents are today."
 
Years later, I watched him at a solar roof construction site with his two - year - old boy known as X.
It was 10:00 PM and there were [cliff](cliff.md) and other moving equipment lift by two spotlights that cast big shadows.
Musk put X on the ground, so the boy could explore on his own, which he did without fear. 
As he [poked](poke.md) around [amid](amid.md) the wires and [cables](cable.md), Musk glanced at him occasionally, but [refrained](refrained.md) from [intervening](intervene.md).
Finally, after X started to climb on a spotlight, Musk walked over and picked him up. 
X [squirmed](squirmed.md) and [squealed](squealed.md), unhappy about being [restrained](restrained.md). 
Musk would later talk about, even joke about having Asperger's, a common name for a form of [autism](autism.md) [spectrum](spectrum.md) disorder that can affect a person's social skills.

**Relationships, emotional connectivity and self-[regulation](regulation.md).
 
He was never [diagnosed](diagnosed.md) as a kid, his mother says, but he says he has Asperger's,and I'm sure he's right. 
The condition was [exacerbated](exacerbate.md) by his childhood [traumas](trauma.md). 
Whenever he would later feel bullied or threatened, his close friend Antonio Gracia says, the PTSD from his childhood would [hijack](hijack.md) his [limbic](limbic.md) system, the part of the brain that control emotional responses. 
As a result, he was bad at picking up social cues.
"I took people literally when they said something," he says. 
"And it was only by reading books that I began to learn that people did not always say what they really meant." 
He had a preference for things that were more precise, such as engineering, physics and coding.

Like all psychological [traits](trait.md), Musk's were complex and individualized. 
He could be very emotional, especially about his own children, and he felt acutely the anxiety that comes from being alone. 
But he didn't have the emotional [receptors](receptor.md) that produce everyday kindness and warmth, and a desire to be liked. 
He was not hardwired to have empathy, or to put it in less technical terms（在不那么专业的说法下）, he could be an asshole.

**The divorce**
May and Ariel Musk were at an Oktoberfest celebration with three other couples, drinking beer and having fun. 
When a guy at another table whistled at May and called her sexy. 
Ariel was [furious](furious.md), but not at the guy. 
The way May remembers it, he [lunged](lunge.md) and was about to hit her, and a friend had to [restrain](restrain.md) him. 
She [fled to](flee%20to.md) her mother's house.

Over time, he had gotten crazier, May later said. 
"He would hit me when the kids were around.
I remember that Elon, who was 5, would hit him on the backs of his knees to try to stop him." 
Ariel calls the [accusations](accusation.md) "absolute rubbish." 
He claims he adored May, and over the years he tried to win her back. 
"I've never laid a hand on a woman in my life, and certainly none of my [wives](wife.md)," he says. 
"That's one of women's weapons is to cry that the man abused her, to cry, and to lie. 
And a man's weapons are to buy, and to [sign](sign.md)."

On the morning after the Octoberfest [altercation](altercation.md), Arrow [came over](comeover) to May's mother's house, apologized, and asked May to come back.
"Don't you dare touch her again," one of Red Haldeman said. 
"If you do, she's coming to live with me." 
May said that he never hit her after that, but his verbal abuse continued.
He would tell her that she was boring, stupid, and ugly. 
The marriage never recovered.

Arrow later admitted it was his fault. 
"I had a very pretty wife, but there were always prettier, younger girls," he said. "I really loved May, but I [screwed up](screw%20up.md)." 
They divorced when Elon was 8.

May and the children moved to a house on the coast near Durban, about 380 miles south of the Pretoria Johannesburg area, where she [juggled](juggled.md) jobs as a model and dietician.
There was little money. She bought her kids second hand books and uniforms.

On some weekends and holidays, the boys—but usually not Tosca—would take the train to see their father in Pretoria. 
"He would send them back without any clothes or bags, so I had to buy them new clothes every time," she says. 
"He said that I would eventually return to him because I would be so [poverty](poverty.md)- [stricken](stricken.md), and wouldn't be able to feed them."

Often, she would have to travel on a modeling job, or to give a nutrition lecture, leaving the kids at home. 
"I never felt guilty about working full time, because I didn't have a choice," she says.
"My children had to be responsible for themselves. 
The freedom taught them to be self-[reliant](reliant.md)." 
When they face a problem, she had a [stock](stock.md) response: "You'll figure it out."

As Campbell recalls, "Mom wasn't soft and [cuddly](cuddly.md), and she was always working. But that was a gift for us." 
Elon developed into a night person, staying up until dawn reading books.
When he saw his mother's light go on at 6:00 AM, he would [crawl](crawl.md) into bed and fall asleep.
That meant she had trouble getting him up in time for school, and on nights when she was away, he would sometimes not get to class until 10:00 a.m.

After getting called from the school, Arrow launched a [custody](custody.md) battle, and had [subpoenas](subpoena.md) issued for Elon's teachers, May's modeling agent, and their neighbors.
[Right before going to trial](right%20before%20trial.md)(美国庭审的一个程序), Arrow dropped the case. 
Every few years, he would [initiate](initiate.md) another court action, and then drop it.

When Tosca recounts these tales, she begins to cry. 
"I remember Mom just sitting there, sobbing on the couch. 
I didn't know what to do. 
All I could do was to hold her."

May and Errol were each drawn to dramatic [intensity](intensity.md) rather than [domestic](domestic.md) [bliss](bliss), a trait they would pass on. 
After her divorce, May began dating another [abusive](abusive.md) man. 
The children hated him and would occasionally put tiny [firecrackers](firecracker.md) in his cigarettes that would [explode](explode.md) when he lit up. 
Soon after the man proposed marriage, he got another woman pregnant. 
"She had been a friend of mine," May says.
"We had modeled together."

# Chapter three,Life with Father,The movie
At age ten, Musk made a fateful decision, one that he would later regret. 
He decided to move in with his father.
He took the dangerous [overnight](overninght.md) train from Durban to Johannesburg on his own. When he spotted his father waiting for him at the station, he began [beaming](beaming.md) with [delight](delight.md) like the sun.
"Hi, dad. Let's get a hamburger," he shouted. 
That night, he crawled into his father's bed and slept there.

Why did he decide to move in with his father? 
Elon [sighs](sigh.md) and stays silent for almost a minute when I ask this. 
"My dad was lonely, so lonely, and I felt I should keep him company," he finally says. 
"He used psychological [wiles](wiles.md) on me."
He also adored his grandmother, Errol's mother, Cora, known as Nana. 
She convinced him that it was unfair that his mother had all three children and his father had none.

In some ways, the move was not all that [mysterious](mysterious.md).
Elon was 10, socially awkward and had no friends. 
His mother was loving, but she was overworked, [distracted](distracted.md) and vulnerable. 
His father, [in contrast](in%20contrast.md), was [swaggering](swaggering.md) and manly, a big guy with large hands and a [mesmerizing](mesmerizing.md) [presence](presence.md). 
His career had many ups and downs, but at that time, he was feeling [flush](flush.md).
He owned a gold colored [convertible](convertible.md) Rolls-Royce Corniche, and more importantly, two sets of [encyclopedias](encyclopedias.md), lots of books and a variety of engineering tools.
So Elon, still a small boy, chose to live with him.

"It turned out to be a really bad idea," he says.
"I didn't yet know how horrible he was."
Four years later, Kimbal followed. "
I didn't want to leave my brother alone with him," 
Kimbal says.
"My dad guilted my brother into going to live with him and then he guilted me."

Why did he choose to go live with someone who [inflicted](inflict.md) pain, May Musk asked 40 years later. 
Why didn't he prefer a happy home? 
Then she paused for a moment. 
"Maybe that's just who he is."

**The Lodge in Timbavati**
After the boys moved in, they helped Errol build a lodge that he could rent to tourists in the Timbavati Game Reserve, a [pristine](pristine.md) [stretch](stretch.md) of bush about 300 miles east of Pretoria. 
During construction, they slept around a fire at night with Browning [rifles](rifles.md) to protect them against lions.
The bricks were made of river sand and the roof was grass.
As an engineer, Errol liked studying the [properties](properties.md) of various materials and he made the floors out of [mica](mica.md) because it was a good [thermal](thermal.md) [insulator](insulator.md). 
Elephants in search of water often [uprooted](uproot.md) the pipes and monkeys regularly broke into the [pavilions](pavilions.md) and [pooped](poop.md). 
So there was a lot of work for the boys to do.
Elon often accompanied visitors on hunts. 
Although he had only a 22 [caliber](caliber.md) rifle, it had a good [scope](scope.md) and he became an expert shot.
He even won a local [skeet](skeet.md) shooting contest, though he was too young to accept the prize of [a case of](a%20case%20of.md) whiskey.

**Trips to America and Hong Kong**
When Elon was 9, his father took him, Kimbal and Tosca on a trip to America, where they drove from New York through the Midwestern West and then down to Florida.
Elon became [hooked on](hook%20on.md) the coin-operated video games he found in the [motel](motel.md) [lobbies](lobby.md).
"It was by far the most exciting thing," he said. 
"We didn't have that yet in South Africa." 
Errol displayed his mix of [flamboyance](flamboyance.md) and [frugality](frugality.md).
He rented a Thunderbird, but they stayed in budget [inns](inn.md).

"When we got to Orlando, my father refused to take us to Disney World because it was too expensive," 
Musk recalls. "I think we went to some water park instead." 
[As is often the case](As%20is%20often%20the%20case.md), Errol spins a different tale, insisting that they went both to Disney World, where Elon liked the haunted house ride, and to Six Flags Over Georgia. 
"I told them over and over on the trip, 'America is where you will come live someday.'"

Two years later, he took the three children to Hong Kong. 
"My father had some [combination](combination.md) of [legitimate](legitimate.md) business and [hucksterism](hucksterism.md),"
Musk recalls. "He left us in the hotel, which was pretty [grungy](grungy.md), and just gave us $50 or something.
And we didn't see him for two days." 
They watched [samurai](samurai.md) movies and cartoons on the hotel TV.
Leaving Tosca behind, Elon and Kimbal wandered the streets, going into electronic stores where they could play video games for free.

"Nowadays, someone would call the child protection service if someone did what our dad did," Musk says. 
"But for us back then, it was a wondrous experience."

**A [Confederacy](Cufederacy.md) of Cousins**
After Elon and Kimbal moved in with their father in [suburban](suburban.md) Pretoria, May moved to nearby Johannesburg so the family could be closer together. 
On Fridays, she would drive to Errol's house to pick up the boys.
They would then go see their grandmother, the [indomitable](indomitable.md) Winifred Haldeman, who cooked the chicken [stew](stew.md) kids hated so much that May would take them out for pizza.

[Afterward](afterward.md), Elon and Kimbal usually spent the night at the house next door to their grandmother's, where May's sister Krive and her three boys lived. 
The five cousins, Elon and Kimbal Musk and Peter, Lyndon and Russ Rive, became an adventurous and occasionally [contentious](contentious.md) herd of [bucks](buck.md).

May was more [indulgent](indulgent.md) and less protective than her sister, so they would [conspire](conspire.md) with her when plotting adventure.
"If we wanted to disappear for the day to do something like go to a concert in Johannesburg, she would say to her sister, 'I'm going to take them to church camp this evening,'" 
says Kimbal. "Then she would drop us off and we would go do our [mischief](mischief.md)."

Those trips could be dangerous.
"I remember once when the train stopped, there was an [immense](immense.md) fight and we watched a guy get [stabbed](stab.md) through the head," 
says Peter Rive. "We were hiding inside the car. 
Then the doors closed and we were like moving on." 
Sometimes a gang would board the train to [hunt down](hunt%20down.md) [rivals](rival.md), [rampaging](rampage.md) through the cars shooting machine guns.

Some of the concerts were anti-apartheid protests, such as one in 1985 in Johannesburg that drew 100,000 people. 
Often [brawls](brawls.md) would [break out](break%20out.md). 
"We didn't try to hide from the violence. 
We became survivors of it," says Kimbal.
"It taught us not to be afraid, but also to not do crazy things."

Elon developed a reputation for being the most fearless.
When the cousins went to a movie and people were making noise, he would be the one to go over and tell them to be quiet, even if they were much bigger. 
"It's a big theme for him: to never have his decisions guided by fear," Peter recalls. 
"That was definitely present even when he was a child."

He was also the most competitive of the cousins. 
One time, when they were riding their bicycles from Pretoria to Johannesburg, Elon was [way out](way%20out.md) in front, [pedaling](pedal.md) fast, so the others [pulled over](pull%20over.md) and [hitchhiked](hitchhike.md) in a [pickup](pickup.md) truck.
When Elon rejoined them, he was so angry that he started hitting them. 
"It was a race," he said, and they had cheated.

Such fights were common. 
Often they would happen in public, the boys [oblivious](oblivious.md) to their surroundings.
One of the many that Elon and Kimbal had was at a country [fair](fair.md). 
They were wrestling and punching each other in the dust, Peter recalls. 
"People were freaking out, and I had to say to the crowd, 'This is not a big deal, these guys are brothers.'"

Although the fights were usually over small things, they could get [vicious](vicious.md). 
"The way to win was to be the first person to punch or kick the other guy in the balls,"
Kimbal says. "That would end the fight, because you can't continue if you get [crunched](crunch.md) in the balls."

**The Student**
Musk was a good student, but not a superstar. 
When he was 9 and 10, he got A's in English and math. 
"He is quick to grasp new mathematical concepts," his teacher noted. 
But there was a constant [refrain](refrain.md) in the report card comments: "He works extremely slowly, either because he dreams or is doing what he should not.
He seldom finishes anything. 
Next year, he must concentrate on his work, and not daydream during class."

His compositions show a lively imagination, but he doesn't always finish in time. His average grade before he got to high school was 83 out of 100. 
After he was bullied and beaten in his public high school, his father moved him to a private academy, Pretoria Boys' High School. 
Based on the English model, it featured strict rules, caning, [compulsory](compulsory.md) [chapel](chapel.md), and uniforms.

There, he got excellent grades in all but two subjects.
Afrikaans: he got 61 out of 100 his final year. 
Religious instruction: "not extending himself," the teacher noted. 
"I wasn't really going to put a lot of effort into things I thought were meaningless," he says.
"I would rather be reading or playing video games."
He got an A in the physics part of his senior certificate exams, but somewhat surprisingly, he got only a B in the math part.

In his spare time, he liked to make small rockets and experiment with different mixtures, such as swimming pool [chlorine](chlorine.md) and [brake](brake.md) [fluid](fluid.md), to see what would make the biggest bang.
He also learned magic tricks and how to [hypnotize](hypnotize.md) people, once convincing Tosca that she was a dog and getting her to eat [raw](raw.md) bacon.

**Early Entrepreneurship and Reading**
As they would later do in America, the cousins [pursued](pursue.md) various entrepreneurial ideas. 
One Easter, they made chocolate eggs, wrapped them in [foil](foil.md), and sold them door to door. 
Kimbal came up with an [ingenious](ingenious.md) [scheme](scheme.md): instead of selling them cheaper than the Easter eggs at the store, they made them more expensive. 
"Some people would [balk](balk.md) at the price," he says, 
"but we told them, 'You're actually supporting future [capitalists](capitalist.md).'"

Reading [remained](remain.md) Musk's psychological [retreat](retreat.md). 
Sometimes he would immerse himself in books all afternoon and most of the night, nine hours at a stretch.
When the family went to someone's house, he would disappear into their host's library. 
When they went into town, he would wander off, and later be found at a bookstore, sitting on the floor in his own world.

He was also deeply into comics;
the [single-minded](single-minded.md) passion of the superheroes impressed him.
"They're always trying to save the world, with their [underpants](underpant.md) on the outside or these skin-tight iron suits, which is really pretty strange when you think about it," he says.
"But they are trying to save the world."

Musk read both sets of his father's encyclopedias, and became, to his [doting](doting.md) mother and sister, a genius boy. 
To other kids, however, he was an annoying nerd.

"Look at the moon, it must be a million miles away," a cousin once exclaimed.  
Replied Elon, "No, it's like 239,000 miles, depending on the orbit."

One book that he found in his father's office described great [inventions](invention.md) that  would be made in the future.
"I would come back from school and go to a side room in my father's office and read it over and over," he said. 
Among the ideas was a rocket [propelled](propell.md) by an [ion](ion.md) [thruster](thruster.md), which would use [particles](particle.md) rather than gas for thrust.

Late one night at the control room of his rocket base in South Texas, Musk described the book [at length](at%20length.md) to me, including how an ion thruster would work in a [vacuum](vacuum.md). 
"That book is what first made me think about going to other planets," he said
# Chapter four,The Seeker:Early Questioning of Religion
**Pretoria, the 1980s.[Existential](existential) crisis.**
When Musk was young, his mother started taking him to [Sunday school](Sunday%20school.md) at the local [Anglican](Anglican.md) church where she was a teacher. It did not go well. 
She would tell her class stories from the [Bible](Bible.md), and he would question them. What do you mean the Waters parted, he asked. 
It's not possible.
When she told the story of Jesus feeding the crowd with [loaves](loaf.md) and fishes, he [countered](counter.md) that things cannot [materialize](materialize.md) out of nothing.
Having been [baptized](baptize.md), he was expected to take [communion](communion.md), but he began questioning that as well. 
I took the blood and body of Christ, which is weird when you're a kid, he says. 
I said, what the hell is this? 
Is this a weird [metaphor](metaphor.md) for [cannibalism](cannibalism.md)?
May decided to let Elon stay home and read on Sunday mornings.

His father, who was more god fearing, told Elon that there were things that could not be known through our limited senses and minds. 
There are no [atheist](atheist.md) pilots, he would say, and Elon would add, there are no atheists at exam time.
But Elon came to believe early on that science could explain things, and so there was no need to [conjure](conjure.md) up a creator or a [deity](deity.md) that would [intervene](intervene.md) in our lives.

**[Adolescent](adolescent.md) Existential Crisis and Turn to Science Fiction**
When he reached his teens, it began to [gnaw](gnaw.md) at him that something was missing. Both the religious and the scientific explanations of existence, he says, did not address the really big questions, such as where did the universe come from, and why does it exist? 
Physics could teach everything about the universe, except why. 
That led to what he calls his adolescent existential crisis. 
I began trying to figure out what the meaning of life and the universe was, he says. 
And I got real depressed about it, like maybe life may have no meaning. 

Like a good bookworm, he addressed these questions through reading.
At first, he made the typical mistake of anxious adolescence and read existential [philosophers](philosophers.md) such as [Nietzsche](Nietzsche.md), [Heidegger](Heidegger.md) and [Schopenhauer](Schopenhauer.md). 
This had the effect of turning confusion into despair.
I do not recommend reading Nietzsche as a teenager, he says. 
Fortunately, he was saved by science fiction, that [wellspring](wellspring.md) of wisdom for game playing kids with [intellects](intellect.md) on [hyperdrive](hyperdrive.md). 
He [ploughed](plough.md) through the entire sci-fi section in his school and local libraries, then pushed the librarians to order more. 

One of his favorites was Robert Heinlein's The Moon is a [Harsh](harsh.md) [Mistress](mistree.md), a novel about a lunar [penal](penal.md) colony. 
It is managed by a supercomputer nicknamed Mike that is able to [acquire](acquire.md) self-awareness and a sense of humor. 
The computer sacrifices its life during a [rebellion](rebellion.md) at the [penal colony](penal%20colony.md). 
The book explores an issue that would become central to Musk's life. 
Will artificial intelligence develop in ways that benefit and protect humanity? 
Or will machines develop intentions of their own and become a threat to humans?
That topic is central to what became another of his favorites, Isaac Asimov's robot stories. 

**Influence of Isaac Asimov's Robot Stories and Zeroeth Law**
The tales [formulate](formulate.md) laws of robotics that are designed to make sure robots do not get out of control. 
In the final scene of his 1985 novel, Robots and Empire, Asimov [expounds](expound.md) the most fundamental of these rules, [dubbed](dub.md) the Zeroeth Law.
A robot may not harm humanity or through [inaction](inaction.md) allow humanity to come to harm.
The heroes of the book develop a plan to send settlers to distant regions of the galaxy in order to preserve human [consciousness](consciousness.md) in the face of an [impending](impending.md) dark age. 
More than 30 years later, Musk [unleash](unleash.md) a random [tweet](tweet.md) about how these ideas motivated his quest to make humans a [spacefaring](spacefaring.md) species and to [harness](harness.md) artificial intelligence to be at the service of humans. 

Foundation series and Zeroeth law are fundamental to creation of SpaceX.
The science fiction book that most influenced his wonder years was Douglas Adams, The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy. 
The [jaunty](jaunty.md) and [wry](wry.md) tale helped shape Musk's [philosophy](philosophy.md) and added a [dollop](dollop.md) of [droll](droll.md) humor to his serious [mien](mien.md). 
The Hitchhiker's Guide, he says, helped me out of my existential depression and I soon realized it was amazingly funny in all sorts of [subtle](subtle.md) ways. 
The story involves a human named Arthur Dent who was rescued by a passing spaceship seconds before the earth is destroyed by an alien civilization that is building a [hyper](hyper.md) space highway. 
[Along with](along%20with.md) his alien rescuer, Dent explores various [nooks](nook.md) and [crannies](cranny.md) of the galaxy, which is run by a two headed president who had turned [unfathomability](unfathomability.md) into an art form. 

The [denizens](denizen.md) of the galaxy are trying to figure out the answer to the ultimate question of life, the universe and everything.
They build a supercomputer, but after more than 7 million years, [spouts](spout.md) out the answer: 42. 
When that [provokes](provoke.md) of a [befuddled](befuddled.md) [howl](howl.md), the computer replies, that quite definitely is the answer.
I think the problem, to be quite honest with you, is that you've never actually known what the question is.
That lesson stuck with Musk. 
I took from the book that we need to extend the scope of consciousness so that we are able to ask the questions about the answer, which is the universe. 

He says The Hitchhiker's Guide, combined with Musk's later [immersion](immersion.md) into video and [tabletop](tabletop.md) [simulation](simulation.md) games, led to a lifelong fascination with the [tantalizing](tantalizing.md) thought that we might nearly be [pawns](pawns.md) in a simulation devised by some higher order beings. 
As Douglas Adams writes, there is a theory which states that if ever anyone discovers exactly what the universe is for and why it is here, it will [instantly](instantly.md) disappear and be replaced by something even more [bizarre](bizarre.md) and [inexplicable](inexplicable.md). 
There is another theory which states that this has already happened.

**Gaming and Early Computer Programming**
In the late 1970s, the role playing game Dungeons and Dragons became a popular [obsession](obsession.md) among the global [tribe](tribe.md) of [geeks](geek). 
Elon Musk and their arrive cousins immersed themselves in the game, which involves sitting around the table and guided by character [sheets](sheet.md) and the role of [dice](dice.md), embarking on fantasy adventures. 
One of the players serves as the dungeon master, refereeing the action. 
Elon Usually played the dungeon master and surprisingly did it with gentleness. Even as a kid, Elon had a whole bunch of different [demeanors](demeanor.md) and moods, says his cousin Peter Rive.

As a dungeon master, he was incredibly patient, which is not in my experience, always his [default](default.md) personality, if you know what I mean. 
It happens sometimes and it's so beautiful when it does. 
Instead of [pressuring](pressuring.md) his brother and cousins, he would turn very [analytical](analytical.md) to describe the options Had in each situation.
Together, they entered a [tournament](tournament.md) in Johannesburg at which they were the youngest players.
The tournament's dungeon master assigned their mission.
You have to save this woman by figuring out who in the game is the bad guy and killing him. 

Elon looked at the dungeon master and said, I think you're the bad guy. 
And so they killed him.
Elon was right and the game, which was supposed to last a few hours, was over. The organizers accused them of [somehow](somehow.md) cheating and at first tried to deny them the prize.
But Musk [prevailed](prevailed.md). 
These guys were idiots, he says. 
It was so obvious. 

Musk saw his first computer around the time he turned eleven.
He was in a shopping mall in Johannesburg and he stood there for minutes just staring at it. 
I had read computer magazines, he says, but I had never actually seen a computer before.
As with the motorcycle, he [hounded](hound.md) his father to get him one.
Errol was [bizarrely](bizarrely.md) [averse](averse.md) to computers, claiming they were good only for time wasting games, not Engineering.
So Elon saved his money from [odd](odd.md) jobs and bought [commodore](commodore.md) v twenty, one of the earliest personal computers. 

It could play games such as [deluxe](deluxe.md) and alpha [blaster](blaster.md), in which a player attempts to protect earth from alien [invaders](invader.md). 
The computer came with the course and how to program in basic. 
That involved sixty hours of lessons. 
I did it in three days, barely sleeping, he remembers.
A few months later, he [tore](tore.md) out an ad for a [conference](conference) on personal computers at a university and told his father he wanted to attend again. 
His father balked. 
It was an expensive [seminar](seminar.md), about four hundred dollars and not [meant](meant.md) for children. 

Elon replied that it was [essential](essential.md), and just stood next to his father staring. 
Over the next few days, Elon would pull the ad out of his pocket and [renew](renew.md) his demand. 
Finally, his father was able to talk the university into giving a discounted price for Elon to stand in the back. 
When Errol came to pick him up at the end, he found Elon engaging with three of the professors. 
This boy must get a new computer, one of the professors said.

**Early Programming Achievements and Game Development**
After he [aced](aced.md) a programming skills test at his school, he got an IBM PC XT, and taught himself to program using Pascal and Turbo C plus plus.
At age thirteen, he was able to create a video game, which he named Blastar, using 123 lines of Basic, and some simple [assembly](assembly.md) language to get the [graphics](graphics.md) to work. 
He [submitted](submitted.md) it to PC and Office Technology magazine, and it appeared in December 1984 issue with a short introduction explaining.

In this game, you have to destroy an alien space [freighter](freighter.md), which is carrying deadly [hydrogen](hydrogen.md) bombs and [status](status.md) [beam](beam.md) machines.
Although it's unclear what a status beam machine is, the concept sounds cool. 
The magazine paid him $500, and he [proceeded](proceed.md) to sell it two other games, one like Donkey Kong, and the other simulating [roulette](roulette.md) and [blackjack](blackjack.md).
Thus began a lifelong [addiction](addiction.md) to video games. 

If you're playing with Elon, you play pretty much nonstop until finally, you have to eat, Peter Rive says.
On one trip to Durban, Elon figured out how to [hack](hack.md) the games in a mall. 
He was able to [hotwire](hotwire.md) the system so that they could play for hours without using any coins.

He then came up with a grand idea. 
The cousins could create a video game [arcade](arcade.md) of their own.
We knew exactly which games were the most popular, so it seemed like a sure thing, Elon says.
He figured out how the cash flow could finance renting the machines.
But when the boys tried to get the city [permits](primits.md), they were told they needed someone over 18 to sign the application.

Kimbal, who had filled out the 30 pages of forms, decided that they couldn't ask Errol. 
He was just too hard of a human, Campbell says. 
So, we went to Russ and Pete's dad, and he [flipped](flip.md) out. 
That basically shut the whole thing down.

# Chapter Five Escape [Velocity](Velocity.md), Leaving South Africa, 1989, Jekyll and Hyde
At age 17, after seven years of living with his father, Elon realized that he would have to escape.
Life with him had become increasingly [unnerving](unnerving.md). 
There were times when Be [jovial](jovial.md) and fun, but occasionally he would become dark, [verbally](verbally.md) abusive and [possessed](possessed.md) by fantasies and [conspiracy](conspiracy.md).
His mood could change on a [dime](dime.md), Tusk says.
"Everything could be [super](super.md), then within a second he would be [vicious](vicious.md) and [spewing](spew.md) abuse. 
It was almost as if he had a [split](split.md) personality."

"One minute he would be super friendly," 
Campbell says, "and the next he would be screaming at you, lecturing you for hours, [Literally](literally.md) two or three hours, while he forced you to just stand there, calling you worse, foolish, pathetic, making staring and evil comments, not allowing you to leave." 
Elon's cousins became [reluctant](reluctant.md) to visit. 
"You never knew what you were in for," 
Peter Rive says. "Sometimes Elon would be like, I just got us some new motorbikes, so let's jump on them. 
At other times, he would be angry and threatening and fuck, make you clean the toilets with a toothbrush." 

When Peter tells me this, he pauses for a moment and then a bit hesitantly notes that Elon sometimes acts this way. 
"When Elon's in a good mood, it's like the coolest, funniest thing in the world. 
And when he's in a bad mood, he goes really dark and you're just walking on [eggshells](eggshell.md)." 

One day, Peter came over to the house and found Errol sitting in his underwear at the kitchen table with a plastic [roulette](roulette.md) wheel. 
He was trying to see whether [microwaves](microwave.md) could affect it. 
He would [spin](spin.md) the wheel, mark down the result, then spin it and put it in a microwave oven and record the result.
"It was [nuts](nuts.md)," Peter says. 
Errol had become convinced that he could find a system for beating the game.
He dragged Elon to the Pretoria Casino many times, dressing him up so that he looked older than 16 and had him write down the numbers while Errol used a calculator hidden under a betting card. 

Elon went to the library and read a few books on [roulette](roulette.md) and even wrote a roulette simulation program on his computer.
He then tried to convince his father that none of his schemes would work. 
But Arrow believed that he had found a deeper truth about probability and as he later described it to me, "an almost total solution to what is called [randomness](randomness.md)."
When I asked him to explain it, he said, "there are no random events or chance. 
All events follow the Fibonacci [sequence](sequence.md) like the [Mandelbrot](Mandelbrot.md) set. 
I went on to discover the relationship between chance and the Fibonacci sequence.
This is the subject for a scientific paper. If I share it, all activities relying on One chance will be ruined. 
So I am in doubt as to doing that." 

I'm not quite sure what all that means. Neither is Elon. 
"I don't know how he went from being greater engineering to believing in [witchcraft](witchcraft.md), but he somehow made that [evolution](evolution.md)." 
Arrow can be very forceful and occasionally convincing. 
"He changes reality around him," Campbell says. 
"He will literally make up things, but he actually believes his own false reality."

Sometimes, Arrow would make [sweeping](sweeping.md) [assertions](assertion.md) to his kids that were unconnected to facts, such as insisting that in the United States, the president is considered [divine](divine.md) and cannot be criticized.
At other times, he would [weave](weave.md) [fanciful](fanciful.md) tales that cast himself as either the hero or the victim. 
All would be [asserted](asserted.md) with such [conviction](conviction.md) that Elon and Campbell would find themselves questioning their own view of real.(such that结构)
"Can you imagine growing up like that," Campbell asks. 
"It was mental [torture](torture.md) and it infects you. 
You end up asking what is reality? I found myself getting caught up in Arrol's tangled web."

In a series of calls and emails over the [course of two years](course%20of%20two%20years.md), he gave me varying [accounts](account.md) of his relationship with and his feelings for his kids, Mae and his stepdaughter with whom he would have two children.
More on that later. "Elon and Campbell have developed their own [narrative](narrative.md) about what I was like and it doesn't accord with the facts," he claims. 
Their tales about him being psychologically abusive, he insists, are told to please their mother. 
But when I [press](press.md) him, he tells me to go with their version. 
"I don't care if they choose a different narrative as long as they are happy. 
I have no desire for it to be my word [versus](versus.md) theirs. [Let them have the floor](Let%20them%20have%20the%20floor.md)."

When talking about his father, Elon will sometimes let loose a laugh, a somewhat harsh and bitter one.
It's similar to the laugh that his father has. 
Some of the words Elon uses, the way he stares, his sudden transitions from light to dark to light, remind his family members of the Arrol [simmering](simmering.md) inside of him.
"I would see shades of these horrible stories Elon told me surface in his own behavior," says Justine, Elon's first wife. 
"It made me realize how difficult it is not to be shaped by what we grew up with, even when that's not what we want.
[Every now and then](every%20now%20and%20then.md), she dared to say something like, 'you're turning into your father,' She explains.
'It was our code phrase to warn him that he was going into the [realm](realm.md) of darkness.'"

But Justine says that Elon, who was always emotionally [invested](invest.md) in their children, is different from his father in a [fundamental](fundamental.md) way. 
"With Aron, there was a sense that really bad things could happen around him.
[Whereas](whereas.md), if the [zombie](zombie.md) [apocalypse](apocalypse.md) happened, you'd want to be on Elon's team, because he would figure out a way to get those zombies [in line](in%20line.md). He can be very harsh, but at the end of the day, you can trust him to find a way to [prevail](prevailed.md)." 

In order for that to happen, he had to move. It was time to leave South Africa.
A one way ticket. 
Musk began pushing both his mother and father, trying to convince them to move to the United States and take him and his [siblings](siblings.md). 
Neither was interested. 
So then I was like, well, I'm just going to go by myself, he says.

He first tried to get US citizenship on the grounds that his mother's father had been born in Minnesota, but that failed because his mother had been born in Canada, and had never claimed US citizenship.
So, he concluded that getting to Canada might be an easier first step.
He went to the Canadian [Consulate](Consulate.md) on his own, got application forms for a passport, and filled them out not only for himself but for his mother, brother, and sister, but not father.
The approvals came through in late May, 1989. 
"I would have left the next morning, but airline tickets were cheaper [back then](back%20then.md) if you bought them 14 days in advance," he says. 
"So, I had to wait those two weeks." 

On June 11th, 1989, about two weeks [shy](shy.md) of his 18th birthday, he had dinner at Pretoria's finest restaurant, Cynthia's, with his father and siblings, who then drove him to the Johannesburg airport.
A few months, Elon's Says his father told him [contemptuously](contemptuously.md), "you'll never be successful." 

As usual, Aron had his own version of the story in which he was the action hero. 
According to him, Elon became seriously depressed during his senior year of high school. 
His despair reached a head on Republic Day, May 31st, 1989. 
His family was preparing to watch the parade, but Elon refused to get out of bed.
His father [leaned](lean.md) against the big desk in Elon's room with its well-used computer and asked, "do you want to go and study in America?" 
Elon [perked](perk.md) up, "yes," he answered. 
Aral claims "it was my idea. 
[Up until then](up%20until%20then.md), he had never said that he wanted to go to America.
So I said, well, tomorrow you should go and see the American Cultural Attaché(美国文化专员), who was a friend of mine from [Rotary](Rotary.md)."

His father's account, Elon says, was just another of his [elaborate](elaborate.md) fantasies casting him as the hero. 
In this case, it was [provably](provably.md) false. 
By [Republic Day](Republic%20Day.md) 1989, Elon had already gotten a Canadian passport and purchased his airline ticket.

# Chapter Six, Canada, 1989. 
***Immigrant.*** 
A [myth](myth.md) has grown that Musk because his father was [on and off](on%20and%20off.md) successful, a lot of money, perhaps pockets filled with emeralds. 
Arrow [at times](at%20time.md) encouraged that [perception](perception.md), but in fact. 
Earl's proceeds from the Zambian animal might have become worthless years earlier. When Elon left South Africa, his father gave him $2,000 in traveler's checks, and his mother provided him with another $2,000 by cashing out a stock account she had opened with the money she won a beauty contest as a teenager.

Otherwise, what he [mainly](mainly.md) had with him when he arrived in Montreal was a list of his mother's relatives he had never met. 
He planned to call his mother's uncle, but discovered that he had left Montreal. 
So, he went to a youth hostel where he shared a room with five other people. 
He was used to South Africa where people wanted the town, [marveling](marveling.md) that people did not have [bars](bars.md) on their windows. 
After a week, he bought a $100 [Greyhound Discovery Pass] 一种公交车票，可以一直旅行that allowed him to travel by bus anywhere in Canada for six months.

He had a second cousin his age, Marc, who lived on a farm in the [Saskatchewan](萨斯喀彻温省.md) province not far from Moose Jaw where his grandparents had moved.
So he headed there.
It was more than 1,700 miles from [Montreal](Montreal.md). 
The bus, which stopped at every [hamlet](hamlet.md), took days to wander across Canada. 
At one stop, he got off to find lunch, and just as the bus was leaving, ran to jump back on.
Unfortunately, the driver had taken off with his [suitcase](suitcase.md) containing his traveler's checks and clothes.
All he had now was the [knapsack](knapsack.md) of books he carried everywhere. 
The difficulty of getting traveler's checks replaced, which took weeks, was an early taste of how the financial payment system needed [disruption](disruption.md).

When he got to the town near his cousin's farm, he used some of the [change](change.md) he had in his pocket to call.
"Hey, it's Elon, your cousin from South Africa," he said. 
"I'm at the bus station." 
The cousin showed up with his father, took him to a [Sizzler](Sizzler.md) [steakhouse](steakhouse.md), and invited him to stay at their [wheat](wheat.md) farm where he was put to work cleaning [grain](grain.md) [bins](bin.md) and helping to raise a [barn](barn.md). 
There, he celebrated his eighteenth birthday with a cake they baked with "Happy Birthday Elon" written in chocolate [icing](icing.md).

After six weeks, he got back on the bus and headed for [Vancouver](Vancouver.md), another thousand miles away, to stay with his mother's half brother.
When he went to an employment office, he saw that most jobs paid $5 an hour, but there was one that paid $18 an hour cleaning out the [boilers](boilers.md) in the [lumber](lumber.md) [mill](mill.md). 
This involved [donning](donning.md) a [hazmat](hazmat.md) suit and [shimmying](shimmying.md) through a small tunnel that led to the [chamber](chamber.md) where the wood [pulp](pulp.md) was being boiled, while [shoveling](shoveling.md) out the line that had [caked](cake.md) on the walls. 
If the person at the end of the tunnel didn't remove the [goo](goo.md) fast enough, he would be trapped while [sweating](sweating.md) his [guts](guts.md) out, he recalled. 
It was like a [Dickensian](Dickensian.md) [steampunk](steampunk.md) [nightmare](nightmare.md) filled with dark pipes and the sound of [jackhammers](jackhammer.md).
**May and Tusk**
While Elon was in [Vancouver](Vancouver.md), May Musk flew from South Africa, having decided that she wanted to move as well. 
She sent back [scouting](scouting.md) reports to [Tuscany](Tuscany.md). 
Vancouver was too cold and rainy, she wrote. 
Montreal was exciting, but people there spoke French.
Toronto, she concluded, was where they should go. 
Tusk [promptly](promptly.md) sold their house and furniture in South Africa, then she joined their mother in Toronto where Elon also moved. 
Kimbal stayed behind in Victoria to finish his last year in high school.

At first, they all lived in a one-bedroom apartment with May and her mother sharing a bed, while Elon slept on the couch. 
There was little money. 
May remembers crying when she spilled some milk because she didn't have enough to buy more.
Tusk got a job at a hamburger joint, Elon as an [intern](intern.md) in Microsoft's Toronto office, and May at the university, modeling agency, and as a diet consultant. 
"I worked every day, and also four nights a week," she says.
"I took off one afternoon, Sunday, to do the [laundry](laundry.md) and get [groceries](groceries.md).
I didn't even know what my kids were doing, because I was hardly at home."

After a few months, they were making enough money to afford rent for a three-bedroom apartment. 
It had felt [wallpaper](wallpaper.md) which May insisted that Elon [ripped](rip.md) down and a [horrid](horrid.md) carpet. They were going to buy a $200 replacement carpet, but Tusk insisted on a [thicker](thicker.md) one for $300, because Campbell and their cousin Peter were coming over to join them and would sleep on the floor. 
Their second big purchase was a computer for Elon. 
He had no friends or social life in Toronto, and he spent most of his time reading or working on the computer. 
Tusk, on the [contrary](contrary.md), was a [saucy](saucy.md) teenager eager to go out. 
"I'm coming with you," Elon would declare.
"Not wanting to be lonely, no, you're not," she would reply. 
But when he insisted, she ordered, "You have to stay 10 feet away from me at all times." He did.
He would walk behind her and her friends, carrying a book to read whenever they went into a club or party.

# Chapter Seven Queens, Kingston, Ontario, 1990-1991
***Industrial relations***

Must college admissions test scores were not especially [notable](notable). 
On the second round of the [SAT](SAT.md) tests, he got a 670 out of 800 on his verbal exam and a 730 on math. 
He narrowed his choices to two universities that were an easy drive from Toronto: [Waterloo](Waterloo.md) and [Queens](Queens.md). 
Waterloo was definitely better for engineering, but it didn't seem great from a social [standpoint](standpoint.md).
He says a few girls there.
